DRILLED SHAFT OBSERVATION REPORT
INTERSTATE ROUTE H 3 FINISH UNIT VIII AND INTERSTATE ROUTE H 1
WAIMALU VIADUCT WIDENING WESTBOUND
CONTRACT NO I
PEARL CITY TO
Dear Mr Hiyakumoto
In accordance with the specifications we provided geotechnical engineering
post design services during the drilled shaft foundation installation for the Waimalu viaduct
widening bridge structure and concrete barrier wall CBW 2 at the above project site This
letter report summarizes our geotechnical observations performed during the drilled shaft
installation for the bridge and barrier wall structures at the project site In general the
purpose of our geotechnical engineering post design services was to observe the drilled
shaft foundation installation in general conformance with the project plans and
specifications and to provide the geotechnical engineering consultation during the
construction
We performed a geotechnical engineering exploration and our recommendations
are presented in our report entitled Geotechnical Engineering Exploration Interstate
Route H 1 Widening Waimalu Viaduct Westbound Pearl City Off Ramp to Kaonohi
Street Pearl City to Aiea Oahu Hawaii dated March 31 2003
One trial shaft and two instrumented load tests were performed at the bridge site
prior to production drilled shaft installation The results of the load testing were presented
in the reports by Loadtest Inc entitled Report On Drilled Shaft Load Testing Osterberg
Method Test Shaft 1 H 1 Waimalu Viaduct Aiea HI dated
and Report On Drilled Shaft Load Testing Osterberg Method Test Shaft 2 H 1
Waimalu Viaduct Aiea HI dated
In addition sonar caliper testing was performed for both load test shafts to obtain
the profile shape and to verify the shaft verticality and diameter of the drilled holes The
results of the sonar caliper testing were presented in the reports by Loadtest Inc entitled
Report on Drilled Shaft Sonar Caliper Testing SCT Test Shaft 1 H 1 Waimalu
Viaduct Aiea HI 1 dated and Report On Drilled Shaft
Sonar Caliper Testing SCT Test Shaft 2 H 1 Waimalu Viaduct Aiea HI

PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
The project consisted of widening the westbound lane of the existing Interstate
Route H 1 Highway from the Pearl City Off Ramp to the Kaonohi Street Overpass from
Pearl City to Aiea on the Island of Oahu Hawaii The project location and general vicinity
are shown on the Project Location Map Plate 1
As part of the highway widening project a new bridge structure was constructed at
the Waimalu Viaduct The new bridge structure consists of 12 spans each span
measured approximately 100 feet from the west to the east including Abutment Nos A
and B and Bent 1 through Bent 11 Based on relatively higher loading demands from the
extreme event limit state and generally soft subsurface conditions a deep foundation
system was adopted to support the new widened bridge structure
Except for Bent 11 the bridge structures are supported on 48 inch or 60 inch
cast in place concrete drilled shaft foundation The approximate locations of the drilled
shafts for the bridge structures are shown on the Drilled Shaft Identification Plans
Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure Plates 2 through 4 Details of the drilled shaft
foundation design parameters are presented on the Summary of As Built Drilled Shafts
Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure Plates 6 1 and 6 2
In addition a new concrete barrier wall CBW was constructed along the edge of
the new widened highway Due to relatively higher design traffic impact loading a portion
of the concrete barrier wall CBW 2 located from Station 102 40 to Station 106 20 is
supported on a deep foundation system The CBW 2 foundation consists of twenty six
concrete shafts A 27 inch D corrugated aluminum pipe CAP was utilized as permanent
casing for the 27 inch shaft installation The CAP was embedded in the new reinforced soil
slope RSS to provide a formed shaft hole and prevent conflict with the geogrids of
reinforcing soil slope RSS
The approximate locations of the shafts for the CBW 2 are shown on the Drilled
Shaft Identification Plan Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2 Plate 5 Details of the shaft
foundation design parameters are presented in the Summary of As Built Drilled Shafts
Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2 Plates 7 1 and 7 2
In general the drilled shafts were designed to derive vertical support primarily from
skin friction The end bearing component of the drilled shafts was discounted in the design
due to difficulties associated with obtaining a clean bottom during construction in relatively
deep drilled holes
SUBSURFACE CONDITIONS
The Waimalu viaduct widening bridge site was generally underlain by a thin surface
fill over soft to stiff recent alluvium and stiff to hard old alluvium The old alluvium was
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
RM Towill Corporation Page 3
W O 4850 10 A
underlain by the extremely to slightly weathered basalt formation A discontinuous layer of
dense to very dense conglomerate approximately 7 to 15 feet thick consisting of
cemented boulders cobbles and gravel was located between the recent alluvium and old
alluvium The thickness of the old alluvium was most pronounced in the areas from Bent 2
to Bent 5 We encountered groundwater at the bridge site at depths ranging from about
8 to 64 below the existing ground surface at the time of the field explorations
At the CBW 2 site the subsurface conditions generally consisted of embankment
fill over soft recent alluvium and weathered basalt formation The thickness of the soft
recent alluvium was on the order of approximate 40 feet We encountered groundwater at
depths of about 15 to 44 feet below the existing ground surface at the time of our field
exploration
DRILLED SHAFT INSTALLATION
To examine construction methods proposed by the contractor and verify the
bearing stratigraphy of the drilled shaft foundations a test program consisting of installing
one trial shaft and installing testing two instrumented load test shafts were performed prior
to the production shaft installation Consequently the production drilled shaft lengths for
the bridge structure were modified based on the results of the instrumented load tests
The following subsections provide descriptions of the test program and discussions
on the production drilled shaft installation
Trial Shaft
A non reinforced 60 inch diameter trial shaft was installed at the designated
location shown on the Drilled Shaft Identification Plan Waimalu Viaduct Widening
Structure Plate 3 The trial shaft was excavated by the drilled shaft contractor
DBM Anderson Drilling Joint Venture from May 27 to The drilled shaft
contractor placed the concrete for the trial shaft on
The drilled shaft contractor used polymer slurry during the excavation of the trial
shaft hole The slurry head was maintained at about 5 to 6 feet above the natural
groundwater level A 65 inch D steel casing was installed to a depth of about 15 feet
below the ground surface A log of the trial shaft and the materials encountered during
shaft excavation are presented in the attached Appendix A Test Drilled Shaft Installation
Records Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure
In general the excavation of the trial shaft penetrated through 40 feet of fill and
recent alluvium 2 feet of conglomerate and 88 feet of weathered basalt formation After
completion of the shaft excavation the drilled hole was backfilled with specified concrete
using tremie method The 65 inch D steel casing was abandoned in place
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
R M Towill Corporation Page 4
W O 4850 10 A
Based on the results of the trial shaft installation the drilled shaft contractor
generally demonstrated that the proposed excavation methods and equipment were
accepted for installing the specified drilled shaft foundations in general accordance with
the project specifications
Load Test Shafts
In accordance with the project specifications two sacrificial instrumented load test
shafts were installed and tested in the designated locations shown on the Drilled Shaft
Identification Plans Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure Plates 2 and 3 The Load Test
Shaft Nos 1 and 2 were excavated by the drilled shaft contractor DBM Anderson Drilling
Joint Venture from June 22 to June 28 and from June 10 to respectively
The load test shafts were extended to depths of about 157 and 145 feet respectively
below the existing ground surface
The drilled shaft contractor used polymer slurry to keep the drilled holes open
during excavation of the load test shafts The 65 inch D steel casing was installed to
depths of about 43 and 59 feet below the ground surface A log of the materials
encountered during shaft excavation and details of the shaft construction are presented in
Appendix A Test Drilled Shaft Installation Records Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure
of this letter report
To obtain the profile shape and verify the verticality and diameter of the drilled
holes Loadtest Inc performed the sonar caliper tests Details of the sonar caliper testing
results are presented in the previously referenced reports prepared by Loadtest Inc
Consequently the drilled shaft contractor lowered the reinforcing cage with an
Osterberg Load Cell and embedment strain gage instrumentation into the drilled holes and
placed concrete in the load test shafts on 1 and for Load Test
Shafts No 1 and 2 respectively
It should be noted that concrete placement for Load Test Shaft No 1 was
temporarily terminated at a depth of about 11 feet below the ground surface on
at about due to concrete shortage Concrete placement resumed
on to a depth of about 2 8 feet below the ground surface Therefore a cold
joint might occur at a depth of about 11 feet below the ground surface Because it was a
sacrificial load test shaft using upward loading of Osterberg load test method we do not
believe that the cold joint would affect the results of the load testing
After the load test shafts were installed and cured for at least six days load testing
was performed by Loadtest Inc The Load Test Shaft No 1 was loaded to the maximum
test load of about 3 066 kips while the Load Test Shaft No 2 was tested to the maximum
test load of about 5 757 kips Details of the load testing results were presented in the
previously referenced reports prepared by Loadtest Inc
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
R M Towill Corporation Page 5
W O 4850 10 A
Based on the results of the sonar caliper tests and Osterberg load tests the
production drilled shaft tip elevations were revised and is shown on the Summary of
As Built Drilled Shafts Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure Plates 6 1 and 6 2
Production Drilled Shafts
A total of 54 production drilled shafts consisting of sixteen 48 inch diameter shafts
at Abutments A and B Bent 9 and replacement shaft at Bent 1 and thirty eight 60 inch
diameter shafts were installed for the widening bridge structure between
and May 18 2005 The approximate drilled shaft locations are shown on the Drilled Shaft
Identification Plans Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure Plates 2 through 4
At the concrete barrier wall CBW 2 site total of 39 production drilled shafts
including twenty six 24 inch diameter shafts and thirteen 27 inch diameter shafts were
installed between and The approximate drilled shaft
locations are shown on the Drilled Shaft Identification Plan Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2
Plate 5
In general Geolabs representatives observed the shaft excavation placement of
the steel reinforcements and concrete placement operations during the installation of the
drilled shafts
Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure
DBM Anderson Drilling Joint Venture constructed the production drilled shafts for
the widening bridge structure using either or SoilMec R 622HD
track mounted drill rigs equipped with various sized augers drilling buckets core
barrels and cleanout buckets Except for shafts installed at Bent 10 and Abutment
B 53 inch and 65 inch D diameter permanent steel casings were utilized for
48 inch and 60 inch diameter shafts respectively to case the upper portions of the
drilled shafts during the shaft construction The production shafts were excavated to
elevations ranging from about 64 to 139 feet Mean Sea Level MSL A summary
of the installed shafts is presented on the Summary of As Built Drilled Shafts
Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure Plates 6 1 and 6 2
The drilled shaft contractor used polymer slurry to keep the uncased portion of the
drilled hole open during excavation while shafts at Abutment B were excavated in a
dry hole condition with weathered basalt rock formation throughout the entire depth
of the excavation The polymer slurry was recycied using on site slurry tanks and
was monitored for viscosity specific gravity sand content and pH value in the
drilled holes A log of the materials encountered during shaft excavation results of
the slurry testing and details of the shaft construction are presented in Appendix B
Production Drilled Shaft Installation Records Waimalu Viaduct Widening
Structure of this letter report
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
R M Towill Corporation Page 6
W O 4850 10 A
It should be noted that classified excavation including standard special rock and
obstruction excavations was specified in the project specifications The standard
excavation was defined as drilling in fill materials and recent alluvium deposits
using conventional drilling tools while the special excavation was defined as drilling
in conglomerate and old alluvium deposits utilizing special drilling tools The rock
excavation was defined as drilling in weathered basalt formation using core barrel
and other tools necessary The obstruction excavation was specified as drilling in
man made materials or structures and boulder materials embedded in the recent
alluvium deposits
After the shaft holes were drilled to their designated tip elevations the reinforcing
rebar cages were placed into the drilled holes Rebar cage spacers were used to
provide the clearance associated with a minimum concrete cover of 4 inches
between the sidewalls of the drilled hole and the sides of the rebar cage
The shaft concrete was placed in the drilled holes through 5 to 10 inch O D steel
pipe by tremie methods where the slurry drilling fluid was used during the
excavation During concrete placement the bottom of the tremie pipe was
immersed in at least 5 feet of concrete as required in the specifications Where the
slurry drilling fluid was not utilized at Abutment B the shaft concrete was placed by
free fall through a drop chute in less than 25 feet in height
The volume of concrete placed in the shaft was monitored and also presented in
Appendix B It should be noted that maximum elapse time of concrete placement
was initially specified as less than 2 hours Due to longer concrete placement time
anticipated the contractor requested for extension of concrete placement time up to
4 hours with slump testing results showing about 4 inches of slump maintained after
4 hours The request was approved with conditions of increasing initial concrete
slump between 8 0 and 9 0 inches and slump loss test in the field for verification
Non destructive concrete integrity testing using Cross hole Sonic Logging CSL
method was performed on the production shafts and concrete coring was
conducted on selected production shafts The results of the integrity testing
indicated that poor quality concrete was encountered at shallow depths varying
from 2 to 9 feet below top of design cut off elevation in some of the production
shafts To mitigate the poor quality concrete encountered in these shafts the
concrete within the defective zones were removed by hoe ram and chipping and
replaced by concrete with the same compressive strength of 4 500 psi at 28 day
age
In addition Shaft No 1 4 at Bent No 1 was installed about 2 5 feet off the design
longitudinal alignment Based on structural engineering re evaluation it was
necessary to install a replacement drilled shaft to compensate for additional
bending moment and torque generated by the eccentricity of the column loads The
replacement shaft was recommended on the mauka side of Bent 1 as shown on
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
R M Towill Corporation Page 7
W O 4850 10 A
Plate 2 Due to relatively lower loading demands the 48 inch diameter replacement
shaft designated as 1 5 was installed to a tip elevation of 86 9 feet MSL
Drilled shaft foundation at Abutment B was also re evaluated due to existing utility
line conflicts Based on relatively hard weathered basalt rock formation throughout
the entire length of the production shafts at Abutment B the number of the
production shafts was reduced from the original six to four
Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2
Two types of production shafts 24 inch and 27 inch diameter were installed to
support the concrete barrier wall CBW 2 Twenty six 24 inch diameter shafts
designated as W 1 through W 26 were excavated by the drilled shaft contractor
Foundation International using a Watson 3000 truck mounted drill rig equipped
with 24 inch auger core barrel and cleanout bucket These 24 inch diameter shafts
were excavated to elevations ranging from about 35 to 44 feet MSL A log of the
materials encountered during shaft excavation and details of the shaft construction
are presented in the attached Appendix C Production Drilled Shaft Installation
Records Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2
Thirteen 27 inch diameter shafts designated as W 27 through W 39 were installed
using 27 inch D corrugated aluminum pipe CAP as permanent casing The CAP
was embedded in new reinforced soil slope RSS to provide formed shaft hole and
prevent conflict with the geogrids in reinforcing soil slope RSS The bottoms of
27 inch shafts were located at elevations ranging from about 36 to 38 feet MSL
Details of the shaft construction are also presented in Appendix C
A summary of the shaft installation is presented in the Summary of As Built Drilled
Shafts Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2 Plates 7 1 and 7 2
It should be noted that the production shafts for CBW 2 were originally specified
During construction the drilled shaft contractor adopted a 24 inch drilling tool for
excavation of the specified 20 inch shafts approximately 15 feet length In addition
drilled shafts W 4 and W 5 were re evaluated due to existing crossing water line
conflicts Drilled shafts W 4 and W 5 were relocated and installed about 5 feet
deeper than the original design tip elevations
The 20 inch diameter shafts were originally designed to embed within residual and
highly weathered basalt rock formation During excavation for Shaft 12
14 18 and 20 hard basalt rock formation was encountered near the bottom of the
drilled holes The excavation for the above shafts were terminated slightly above
the design tip elevations on the order of about 1 foot as shown in the Summary of
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
R M Towill Corporation Page 8
W O 4850 10 A
Based on our field observations we believe that the drilled shafts for the
Waimalu Viaduct Widening Structure and Concrete Barrier Wall CBW 2 have been
installed in general conformance with the project plans and specifications and
within the limits of generally accepted construction practices and the design intents
Based on our observations of the drilled shaft installation it is our professional
Opinion that the drilled shafts have been installed to sufficient depths to provide the
design load capacity
LIMITATIONS
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site Our observation and consultation services
were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of geotechnical
engineering practice no warranty is expressed or implied Provision of construction
monitoring by an engineer is not insurance nor does it guarantee construction of any type
The contractor shall retain primary responsibility for the quality of the work for adhering to
plans and specifications and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found
It should be noted that the drilled shaft plans included in this letter report are not
as built plans The actual location and the top elevation of the shafts should be measured
using optical survey equipment to verify whether the shaft position is within the tolerance in
the project specifications

Standard excavation is measured from the top of shaft to the bottom of shaft designated as standard excavation to the nearest foot discounting the depths from any material removed as
an obstruction within standard excavation
Special excavation is measured from the top of shaft designated as special excavation and the bottom of shaft designated as special excavation to the nearest foot discounting the
depths from any material removed as an obstruction within special excavation
Rock excavation is measured from the top of shaft designated as rock excavation to the bottom of shaft designated as rock excavation to the nearest foot
Drilled shaft is measured only from the top of shaft to final bottom of shaft
Design tip elevation of the drilled shafts were revised based on results of the load tests and shown in Geolabs memoranda dated 29 and August 2 9
Details of drilled shaft installation are presented in the Drilled Shaft Records
Shaft No 1 5 was installed without cost to the State due to excessive mis alignment of Shaft No 1 4
Drilled shaft foundation supporting Abutment B was re evaluated due to the utility conflict and number of the shaft was changed from original 6 to 4
W O 4850 10
